rejects all Nodes, the scheduler would NOT set a failure status to every Node,\n   122→// but set a failure status as AbsentNodesStatus.\n   123→// You're supposed to get a status from AbsentNodesStatus(), and consider all other nodes that are rejected by them.\n   124→func (m *NodeToStatus) ForEachExplicitNode(fn func(nodeName string, status *Status)) {\n   125→\tfor nodeName, code.\n   131→// If the absentNodesStatus matches the code, all existing nodes are fetched using nodeLister\n   132→// and filtered using NodeToStatus.Get.\n   133→// If the absentNodesStatus doesn't match the code, nodeToStatus map is used to create a list of nodes\n   134→// and nodeLister.Get is used to obtain NodeInfo for each.\n   135→func (m *NodeToStatus) NodesForStatusCode(nodeLister NodeInfoLister, code Code) ([]*NodeInfo, error) {\n   136→\tvar resultNodes []*NodeInfo\n   137→\n   138→\tif m.AbsentNodesStatus().Code() == code {\n   139→\t\tallNodes, err := nodeLister.List()\n   140→\t\tif err != nil {\n   141→\t\t\treturn nil, err\n   142→\t\t}\n   143→\t\tif m.Len() == 0 {\n   144→\t\t\t// All nodes are absent and status code is matching, so can return all nodes.\n   145→\t\t\treturn allNodes, nil\n   146→\t\t}\n   147→\t\t// Need to find all the nodes that are absent or have a matching code using the allNodes.\n   148→\t\tfor _, node := range allNodes {\n 154→\t\treturn resultNodes, nil\n   155→\t}\n   156→\n   157→\tm.ForEachExplicitNode(func(nodeName string, status *Status) {\n   158→\t\tif status.Code() == code {\n   159→\t\t\tif nodeInfo, err := 167→\n   168→// NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\n   169→type NodePluginScores struct {\n   170→\t// Name is node name.\n   171→\tName string\n   172→\t// Scores 185→// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\n   186→type Code int\n   187→\n   188→// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n   189→// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\n   190→const (\n   191→\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n   192→\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n   193→\tSuccess Code = iota\n   194→\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n   195→\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n   196→\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n   197→\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n   198→\tError\n   199→\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n   200→\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n   201→\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n   202→\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n   203→\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n   204→\t//\n   205→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   206→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n   207→\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n   208→\tUnschedulable\n   209→\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n   210→\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n   211→\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n   212→\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n   213→\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n   214→\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n   215→\t//\n   216→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   217→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n   218→\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n   219→\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n   220→\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n   221→\tWait\n   222→\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n   223→\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n   224→\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n   225→\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n   226→\tSkip\n   227→\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n   228→\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n   229→\t//\n   230→\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n   231→\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n   232→\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n   233→\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n   234→\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n   235→\t//\n   236→\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n   237→\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n   238→\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n   239→\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n   240→\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n   241→\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n   242→\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n   243→\tPending\n   244→)\n   245→\n   246→// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\n   247→var codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n   248→\n   249→func (c Code) String() string {\n   250→\treturn codes[c]\n   251→}\n   252→\n   253→const (\n   254→\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n   255→\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\n   256→\n   257→\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n   258→\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\n   259→\n   260→\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n   261→\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n   262→)\n   263→\n   264→// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n   265→// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n   266→// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n   267→// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n   268→// - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\n   269→var PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n   270→\n   271→// PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\n   272→type PodsToActivate struct {\n   273→\tsync.Mutex\n   274→\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\n   275→\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\n   276→}\n   277→\n   278→// Clone just returns the same state.\n   279→func (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\n   280→\treturn s\n   281→}\n   282→\n   283→// NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\n   284→func NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n   285→\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n   286→}\n   287→\n   288→// Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n   289→// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n   290→// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n   291→// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n   292→// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\n   293→type Status struct {\n   294→\tcode    Code\n   295→\treasons []string\n   296→\terr     error\n   297→\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n   298→\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n   299→\tplugin string\n   300→}\n   301→\n   302→func (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n   303→\ts.err = err\n   304→\treturn s\n   305→}\n   306→\n   307→// Code returns code of the Status.\n   308→func (s *Status) Code() Code {\n   309→\tif s == nil {\n   310→\t\treturn Success\n   311→\t}\n   312→\treturn s.code\n   313→}\n   314→\n   315→// Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n   316→func (s *Status) Message() string {\n   317→\tif s == nil {\n   318→\t\treturn \"\"\n   319→\t}\n   320→\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n   321→}\n   322→\n   323→// SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\n   324→func (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n   325→\ts.plugin = plugin\n   326→}\n   327→\n   328→// WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n   329→// and returns the given status object.\n   330→func (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n   331→\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n   332→\treturn s\n   333→}\n   334→\n   335→// Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\n   336→func (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n   337→\treturn s.plugin\n   338→}\n   339→\n   340→// Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\n   341→func (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n   342→\tif s.err != nil {\n   343→\t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n   344→\t}\n   345→\treturn s.reasons\n   346→}\n   347→\n   348→// AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\n   349→func (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n   350→\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n   351→}\n   352→\n   353→// IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\n   354→func (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n   355→\treturn s.Code() == Success\n   356→}\n   357→\n   358→// IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\n   359→func (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n   360→\treturn s.Code() == Wait\n   361→}\n   362→\n   363→// IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\n   364→func (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n   365→\treturn s.Code() == Skip\n   366→}\n   367→\n   368→// IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\n   369→func (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n   370→\tcode := s.Code()\n   371→\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n   372→}\n   373→\n   374→// AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n   375→// with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\n   376→func (s *Status) AsError() error {\n   377→\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n   378→\t\treturn nil\n   379→\t}\n   380→\tif s.err != nil {\n   381→\t\treturn s.err\n   382→\t}\n   383→\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n   384→}\n   385→\n   386→// Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n   387→// cmp.Equal.\n   388→func (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n   389→\tif s == nil || x == nil {\n   390→\t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n   391→\t}\n   392→\tif s.code != x.code {\n   393→\t\treturn false\n   394→\t}\n   395→\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n   396→\t\treturn false\n   397→\t}\n   398→\tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n   399→\t\treturn false\n   400→\t}\n   401→\treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n   402→}\n   403→\n   404→func (s *Status) String() string {\n   405→\treturn s.Message()\n   406→}\n   407→\n   408→// NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\n   409→func NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n   410→\ts := &Status{\n   411→\t\tcode:    code,\n   412→\t\treasons: reasons,\n   413→\t}\n   414→\treturn s\n   415→}\n   416→\n   417→// AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\n   418→func AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n   419→\tif err == nil {\n   420→\t\treturn nil\n   421→\t}\n   422→\treturn &Status{\n   423→\t\tcode: Error,\n   424→\t\terr:  err,\n   425→\t}\n   426→}\n   427→\n   428→// WaitingPod represents a pod currently waiting in the permit phase.\n   429→type WaitingPod interface {\n   430→\t// GetPod returns a reference to the waiting pod.\n   431→\tGetPod() *v1.Pod\n   432→\t// GetPendingPlugins returns a list of pending Permit plugin's name.\n   433→\tGetPendingPlugins() []string\n   434→\t// Allow declares the waiting pod is allowed to be scheduled by the plugin named as \"pluginName\".\n   435→\t// If this is the last remaining plugin to allow, then a success signal is delivered\n   436→\t// to unblock the pod.\n   437→\tAllow(pluginName string)\n   438→\t// Reject declares the waiting pod unschedulable.\n   439→\tReject(pluginName, msg string)\n   440→}\n   441→\n   442→// Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\n   443→type Plugin interface {\n   444→\tName() string\n   445→}\n   446→\n   447→// PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n   448→// These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n   449→// Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n   450→// involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n   451→// Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\n   452→type PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n   453→\tPlugin\n   454→\t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n   455→\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n   456→}\n   457→\n   458→// LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\n   459→type LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n   460→\n   461→// QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n   462→// These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n   463→// plugin may be enabled at a time.\n   464→type QueueSortPlugin interface {\n   465→\tPlugin\n   466→\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n   467→\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n   468→}\n   469→\n   470→// EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n   471→// move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n   472→// In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n   473→// and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n   474→// Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n   475→// and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n   476→// This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n   477→// and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n   478→//\n   479→// Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n   480→// otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n   481→// And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\n   482→type EnqueueExtensions interface {\n   483→\tPlugin\n   484→\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n   485→\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n   486→\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n   487→\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n   488→\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n   489→\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n   490→\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n   491→\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n   492→\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n   493→\t//\n   494→\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n   495→\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n   496→}\n   497→\n   498→// PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n   499→// callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n   500→// state.\n   501→type PreFilterExtensions interface {\n   502→\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n   503→\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n   504→\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   505→\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n   506→\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n   507→\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   508→}\n   509→\n   510→// PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n   511→// These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\n   512→type PreFilterPlugin interface {\n   513→\tPlugin\n   514→\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n   515→\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n   516→\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n   517→\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n   518→\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n   519→\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n   520→\t//\n   521→\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n   522→\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n   523→\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n   524→\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n   525→\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n   526→\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n   527→\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n   528→\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n   529→\t// Filter again on a specific node.\n   530→\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n   531→}\n   532→\n   533→// FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n   534→// filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n   535→// This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n   536→// These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n   537→// However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n   538→// Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n   539→// running the pod.\n   540→type FilterPlugin interface {\n   541→\tPlugin\n   542→\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n   543→\t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n   544→\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n   545→\t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n   546→\t//\n   547→\t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n   548→\t//\n   549→\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n   550→\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n   551→\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n   552→\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n   553→\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n   554→\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n   555→\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n   556→\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n   557→}\n   558→\n   559→// PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n   560→// after a pod cannot be scheduled.\n   561→type PostFilterPlugin interface {\n   562→\tPlugin\n   563→\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n   564→\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n   565→\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n   566→\t//\n   567→\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n   568→\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n   569→\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n   570→\t//\n   571→\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n   572→\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n   573→\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n   574→\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n   575→\t//\n   576→\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n   577→\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n   578→\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n   579→\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n   580→\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n   581→}\n   582→\n   583→// PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n   586→// state or to generate logs/metrics.\n   587→type PreScorePlugin interface {\n   588→\tPlugin\n   589→\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n   590→\t// passed the filtering phase. NodeToStatus contains the statuses of the Nodes where the incoming Pod was not schedulable.\ntype NodeToStatus struct {\n\t// nodeToStatus contains specific statuses of the nodes.\n\tnodeToStatus registered,\n// and hence may not run the fn for all existing nodes.\n// For example, if PreFilter rejects all Nodes, the scheduler would NOT set a failure status to every Node,\n// but set a failure status as AbsentNodesStatus.\n// You're supposed to get a status from AbsentNodesStatus(), and consider all other nodes that are rejected by them.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) ForEachExplicitNode(fn func(nodeName string, status *Status)) {\n\tfor nodeName, status := range m.nodeToStatus {\n\t\tfn(nodeName, status)\n\t}\n}\n\n// NodesForStatusCode returns a list of NodeInfos for the nodes that doesn't match the code, nodeToStatus map is used to create a list of nodes\n// and nodeLister.Get is used to obtain NodeInfo for each.\nfunc (m *NodeToStatus) NodesForStatusCode(nodeLister code {\n\t\t\t\tresultNodes = append(resultNodes, node)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\treturn resultNodes, nil\n\t}\n\n\tm.ForEachExplicitNode(func(nodeName string, status *Status) {\n\t\tif status.Code() == NodePluginScores is a struct with node name and scores for that node.\ntype NodePluginScores struct {\n\t// Name is node name.\n\tName string\n\t// Scores is scores from plugins and extenders.\n\tScores []PluginScore\n\t// TotalScore is the total score in Scores.\n\tTotalScore int64\n}\n\n// PluginScore is a struct with plugin/extender name and score.\ntype PluginScore struct {\n\t// Name is the name of plugin or extender.\n\tName  string\n\tScore int64\n}\n\n// Code is the Status code/type which is returned from plugins.\ntype Code int\n\n// These are predefined codes used in a Status.\n// Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\nconst (\n\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\n\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \"Success\".\n\tSuccess Code = iota\n\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\n\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\n\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\n\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\n\tError\n\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\n\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\n\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\n\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulable\n\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\n\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\n\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this status.\n\t// Plugins should return Unschedulable if it is possible that the pod can get scheduled\n\t// after running other postFilter plugins.\n\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\n\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\n\tWait\n\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\n\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\n\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\n\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\n\tSkip\n\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\n\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\n\t//\n\t// For example, the DRA plugin sometimes needs to wait for the external device driver\n\t// to provision the resource for the Pod.\n\t// It's different from when to return Unschedulable/UnschedulableAndUnresolvable,\n\t// because in this case, the scheduler decides where the Pod can go successfully,\n\t// but we need to wait for the external component to do something based on that scheduling result.\n\t//\n\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\n\t// In the case of returning Pending, we cannot say the scheduling cycle is wasted\n\t// because the scheduling result is used to proceed the Pod's scheduling forward,\n\t// that particular scheduling cycle is failed though.\n\t// So, Pods rejected by such reasons don't need to suffer a penalty (backoff).\n\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Pending in the last scheduling,\n\t// the Pod goes to activeQ directly ignoring backoff.\n\tPending\n)\n\n// This list should be exactly the same as the codes iota defined above in the same order.\nvar codes = []string{\"Success\", \"Error\", \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\", \"Wait\", \"Skip\", \"Pending\"}\n\nfunc (c Code) String() string {\n\treturn codes[c]\n}\n\nconst (\n\t// MaxNodeScore is the maximum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMaxNodeScore int64 = 100\n\n\t// MinNodeScore is the minimum score a Score plugin is expected to return.\n\tMinNodeScore int64 = 0\n\n\t// MaxTotalScore is the maximum total score.\n\tMaxTotalScore int64 = math.MaxInt64\n)\n\n// PodsToActivateKey is a reserved state key for stashing pods.\n// If the stashed pods are present in unschedulablePods or backoffQ，they will be\n// activated (i.e., moved to activeQ) in two phases:\n// - end of a scheduling cycle if it succeeds (will be cleared from `PodsToActivate` if activated)\n// - end of a binding cycle if it succeeds\nvar PodsToActivateKey StateKey = \"kubernetes.io/pods-to-activate\"\n\n// PodsToActivate stores pods to be activated.\ntype PodsToActivate struct {\n\tsync.Mutex\n\t// Map is keyed with namespaced pod name, and valued with the pod.\n\tMap map[string]*v1.Pod\n}\n\n// Clone just returns the same state.\nfunc (s *PodsToActivate) Clone() StateData {\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// NewPodsToActivate instantiates a PodsToActivate object.\nfunc NewPodsToActivate() *PodsToActivate {\n\treturn &PodsToActivate{Map: make(map[string]*v1.Pod)}\n}\n\n// Status indicates the result of running a plugin. It consists of a code, a\n// message, (optionally) an error, and a plugin name it fails by.\n// When the status code is not Success, the reasons should explain why.\n// And, when code is Success, all the other fields should be empty.\n// NOTE: A nil Status is also considered as Success.\ntype Status struct {\n\tcode    Code\n\treasons []string\n\terr     error\n\t// plugin is an optional field that records the plugin name causes this status.\n\t// It's set by the framework when code is Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable or Pending.\n\tplugin string\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) WithError(err error) *Status {\n\ts.err = err\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Code returns code of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Code() Code {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn Success\n\t}\n\treturn s.code\n}\n\n// Message returns a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Message() string {\n\tif s == nil {\n\t\treturn \"\"\n\t}\n\treturn strings.Join(s.Reasons(), \", \")\n}\n\n// SetPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin.\nfunc (s *Status) SetPlugin(plugin string) {\n\ts.plugin = plugin\n}\n\n// WithPlugin sets the given plugin name to s.plugin,\n// and returns the given status object.\nfunc (s *Status) WithPlugin(plugin string) *Status {\n\ts.SetPlugin(plugin)\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// Plugin returns the plugin name which caused this status.\nfunc (s *Status) Plugin() string {\n\treturn s.plugin\n}\n\n// Reasons returns reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) Reasons() []string {\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn append([]string{s.err.Error()}, s.reasons...)\n\t}\n\treturn s.reasons\n}\n\n// AppendReason appends given reason to the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AppendReason(reason string) {\n\ts.reasons = append(s.reasons, reason)\n}\n\n// IsSuccess returns true if and only if \"Status\" is nil or Code is \"Success\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSuccess() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Success\n}\n\n// IsWait returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Wait\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsWait() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Wait\n}\n\n// IsSkip returns true if and only if \"Status\" is non-nil and its Code is \"Skip\".\nfunc (s *Status) IsSkip() bool {\n\treturn s.Code() == Skip\n}\n\n// IsRejected returns true if \"Status\" is Unschedulable (Unschedulable, UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, or Pending).\nfunc (s *Status) IsRejected() bool {\n\tcode := s.Code()\n\treturn code == Unschedulable || code == UnschedulableAndUnresolvable || code == Pending\n}\n\n// AsError returns nil if the status is a success, a wait or a skip; otherwise returns an \"error\" object\n// with a concatenated message on reasons of the Status.\nfunc (s *Status) AsError() error {\n\tif s.IsSuccess() || s.IsWait() || s.IsSkip() {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\tif s.err != nil {\n\t\treturn s.err\n\t}\n\treturn errors.New(s.Message())\n}\n\n// Equal checks equality of two statuses. This is useful for testing with\n// cmp.Equal.\nfunc (s *Status) Equal(x *Status) bool {\n\tif s == nil || x == nil {\n\t\treturn s.IsSuccess() && x.IsSuccess()\n\t}\n\tif s.code != x.code {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.err, x.err, cmpopts.EquateErrors()) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\tif !cmp.Equal(s.reasons, x.reasons) {\n\t\treturn false\n\t}\n\treturn cmp.Equal(s.plugin, x.plugin)\n}\n\nfunc (s *Status) String() string {\n\treturn s.Message()\n}\n\n// NewStatus makes a Status out of the given arguments and returns its pointer.\nfunc NewStatus(code Code, reasons ...string) *Status {\n\ts := &Status{\n\t\tcode:    code,\n\t\treasons: reasons,\n\t}\n\treturn s\n}\n\n// AsStatus wraps an error in a Status.\nfunc AsStatus(err error) *Status {\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\treturn &Status{\n\t\tcode: Error,\n\t\terr:  err,\n\t}\n}\n\n// WaitingPod represents a pod currently waiting in the permit phase.\ntype WaitingPod interface {\n\t// GetPod returns a reference to the waiting pod.\n\tGetPod() *v1.Pod\n\t// GetPendingPlugins returns a list of pending Permit plugin's name.\n\tGetPendingPlugins() []string\n\t// Allow declares the waiting pod is allowed to be scheduled by the plugin named as \"pluginName\".\n\t// If this is the last remaining plugin to allow, then a success signal is delivered\n\t// to unblock the pod.\n\tAllow(pluginName string)\n\t// Reject declares the waiting pod unschedulable.\n\tReject(pluginName, msg string)\n}\n\n// Plugin is the parent type for all the scheduling framework plugins.\ntype Plugin interface {\n\tName() string\n}\n\n// PreEnqueuePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreEnqueue\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n// Note: an preEnqueue plugin is expected to be lightweight and efficient, so it's not expected to\n// involve expensive calls like accessing external endpoints; otherwise it'd block other\n// Pods' enqueuing in event handlers.\ntype PreEnqueuePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreEnqueue is called prior to adding Pods to activeQ.\n\tPreEnqueue(ctx context.Context, p *v1.Pod) *Status\n}\n\n// LessFunc is the function to sort pod info\ntype LessFunc func(podInfo1, podInfo2 *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n\n// QueueSortPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"QueueSort\" plugins.\n// These plugins are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue. Only one queue sort\n// plugin may be enabled at a time.\ntype QueueSortPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Less are used to sort pods in the scheduling queue.\n\tLess(*QueuedPodInfo, *QueuedPodInfo) bool\n}\n\n// EnqueueExtensions is an optional interface that plugins can implement to efficiently\n// move unschedulable Pods in internal scheduling queues.\n// In the scheduler, Pods can be unschedulable by PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins,\n// and Pods rejected by these plugins are requeued based on this extension point.\n// Failures from other extension points are regarded as temporal errors (e.g., network failure),\n// and the scheduler requeue Pods without this extension point - always requeue Pods to activeQ after backoff.\n// This is because such temporal errors cannot be resolved by specific cluster events,\n// and we have no choose but keep retrying scheduling until the failure is resolved.\n//\n// Plugins that make pod unschedulable (PreEnqueue, PreFilter, Filter, Reserve, and Permit plugins) should implement this interface,\n// otherwise the default implementation will be used, which is less efficient in requeueing Pods rejected by the plugin.\n// And, if plugins other than above extension points support this interface, they are just ignored.\ntype EnqueueExtensions interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// EventsToRegister returns a series of possible events that may cause a Pod\n\t// failed by this plugin schedulable. Each event has a callback function that\n\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\n\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\n\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\n\t// When it returns an error, the scheduler fails to start.\n\t// Note: the returned list needs to be determined at a startup,\n\t// and the scheduler only evaluates it once during start up.\n\t// Do not change the result during runtime, for example, based on the cluster's state etc.\n\t//\n\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\n\tEventsToRegister(context.Context) ([]ClusterEventWithHint, error)\n}\n\n// PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\n// callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\n// state.\ntype PreFilterExtensions interface {\n\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\n\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\n\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"PreFilter\" plugins.\n// These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\ntype PreFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. All PreFilter\n\t// plugins must return success or the pod will be rejected. PreFilter could optionally\n\t// return a PreFilterResult to influence which nodes to evaluate downstream. This is useful\n\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n\t//\n\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n\t// or nil if it does not. A Pre-filter plugin can provide extensions to incrementally\n\t// modify its pre-processed info. The framework guarantees that the extensions\n\t// AddPod/RemovePod will only be called after PreFilter, possibly on a cloned\n\t// CycleState, and may call those functions more than once before calling\n\t// Filter again on a specific node.\n\tPreFilterExtensions() PreFilterExtensions\n}\n\n// FilterPlugin is an interface for Filter plugins. These plugins are called at the\n// filter extension point for filtering out hosts that cannot run a pod.\n// This concept used to be called 'predicate' in the original scheduler.\n// These plugins should return \"Success\", \"Unschedulable\" or \"Error\" in Status.code.\n// However, the scheduler accepts other valid codes as well.\n// Anything other than \"Success\" will lead to exclusion of the given host from\n// running the pod.\ntype FilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Filter is called by the scheduling framework.\n\t// All FilterPlugins should return \"Success\" to declare that\n\t// the given node fits the pod. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n\t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n\t//\n\t// \"Error\" aborts pod scheduling and puts the pod into the backoff queue.\n\t//\n\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. These plugins are called\n// after a pod cannot be scheduled.\ntype PostFilterPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PostFilter is called by the scheduling framework\n\t// when the scheduling cycle failed at PreFilter or Filter by Unschedulable or UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t// NodeToStatusReader has statuses that each Node got in PreFilter or Filter phase.\n\t//\n\t// If you're implementing a custom preemption with PostFilter, ignoring Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is the responsibility of your plugin,\n\t// meaning NodeToStatusReader could have Nodes with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n\t// and the scheduling framework does call PostFilter plugins even when all Nodes in NodeToStatusReader are UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n\t//\n\t// A PostFilter plugin should return one of the following statuses:\n\t// - Unschedulable: the plugin gets executed successfully but the pod cannot be made schedulable.\n\t// - Success: the plugin gets executed successfully and the pod can be made schedulable.\n\t// - Error: the plugin aborts due to some internal error.\n\t//\n\t// Informational plugins should be configured ahead of other ones, and always return Unschedulable status.\n\t// Optionally, a non-nil PostFilterResult may be returned along with a Success status. For example,\n\t// a preemption plugin may choose to return nominatedNodeName, so that framework can reuse that to update the\n\t// preemptor pod's .spec.status.nominatedNodeName field.\n\tPostFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, filteredNodeStatusMap NodeToStatusReader) (*PostFilterResult, *Status)\n}\n\n// PreScorePlugin is an interface for \"PreScore\" plugin. PreScore is an\n// informational extension point. Plugins will be called with a list of nodes\n// that passed the filtering phase. A plugin may use this data to update internal\n// state or to generate logs/metrics.\ntype PreScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// PreScore is called by the scheduling framework after a list of nodes\n\t// passed the filtering phase. All prescore plugins must return success or\n\t// the pod will be rejected\n\t// When it returns Skip status, other fields in status are just ignored,\n\t// and coupled Score plugin will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n\tPreScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodes []*NodeInfo) *Status\n}\n\n// ScoreExtensions is an interface for Score extended functionality.\ntype ScoreExtensions interface {\n\t// NormalizeScore is called for all node scores produced by the same plugin's \"Score\"\n\t// method. A successful run of NormalizeScore will update the scores list and return\n\t// a success status.\n\tNormalizeScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, scores NodeScoreList) *Status\n}\n\n// ScorePlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Score\" plugins to rank\n// nodes that passed the filtering phase.\ntype ScorePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Score is called on each filtered node. It must return success and an integer\n\t// indicating the rank of the node. All scoring plugins must return success or\n\t// the pod will be rejected.\n\tScore(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (int64, *Status)\n\n\t// ScoreExtensions returns a ScoreExtensions interface if it implements one, or nil if does not.\n\tScoreExtensions() ScoreExtensions\n}\n\n// ReservePlugin is an interface for plugins with Reserve and Unreserve\n// methods. These are meant to update the state of the plugin. This concept\n// used to be called 'assume' in the original scheduler. These plugins should\n// return only Success or Error in Status.code. However, the scheduler accepts\n// other valid codes as well. Anything other than Success will lead to\n// rejection of the pod.\ntype ReservePlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Reserve is called by the scheduling framework when the scheduler cache is\n\t// updated. Permit\n\t// plugins are used to prevent or delay the binding of a Pod. A permit plugin\n\t// must return success or wait with timeout duration, or the pod will be rejected.\n\t// The pod will also be rejected if the wait timeout or the pod is rejected while\n\t// waiting. Note that if the plugin returns \"wait\", the framework will wait only\n\t// after running the remaining plugins given that no other plugin rejects the pod.\n\tPermit(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) (*Status, time.Duration)\n}\n\n// BindPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \"Bind\" plugins. Bind\n// plugins are used to bind a pod to a Node.\ntype BindPlugin interface {\n\tPlugin\n\t// Bind plugins will not be called until all pre-bind plugins have completed. Each\n\t// bind plugin is called in the configured order. A bind plugin may choose whether\n\t// or not to handle the given Pod. If a bind plugin returns an Error, the\n\t// pod is rejected and will not be bound.\n\tBind(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod, nodeName string) *Status\n}\n\n// Framework manages the set of plugins in use by the scheduling framework.\n// Configured plugins are called at specified points in a scheduling context.\ntype Framework interface {\n\tHandle\n\n\t// PreEnqueuePlugins returns the registered preEnqueue plugins.\n\tPreEnqueuePlugins() []PreEnqueuePlugin\n\n\t// EnqueueExtensions returns the registered Enqueue extensions.\n\tEnqueueExtensions() []EnqueueExtensions\n\n\t// QueueSortFunc returns the function to sort pods in scheduling queue\n\tQueueSortFunc() LessFunc\n\n\t// RunPreFilterPlugins runs the set of configured PreFilter plugins. *PreFilterResult {\n\tif p.AllNodes() && in.AllNodes() {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tr := PreFilterResult{}\n\tif p.AllNodes() {\n\t\tr.NodeNames = in.NodeNames.Clone()\n\t\treturn &r\n\t}\n\tif {\n\tif ni == nil {\n\t\treturn ModeNoop\n\t}\n\treturn ni.NominatingMode\n}\n\n// PodActivator abstracts operations in the scheduling queue.\ntype PodActivator interface {\n\t// Activate moves the If a plugin with the same name\n// exists, it returns an error.\nfunc (r Registry) Register(name string, factory PluginFactory) error {\n\tif _, ok := r[name]; ok {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"a plugin named %v already exists\", name)\n\t}\n\tr[name] = factory\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Unregister removes an existing plugin from the registry. If no plugin with\n// the provided name exists, it returns an error.\nfunc (r Registry) Unregister(name string) error {\n\tif _, ok := r[name]; !ok {\n\t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"no plugin named %v exists\", name)\n\t}\n\tdelete(r, name)\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// Merge merges the provided registry to the current one.\nfunc (r Registry) Merge(in Registry) error {\n\tfor name, factory := range in {\n\t\tif err := r.Register(name, factory); err != nil {\n\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn nil\n}\n","numLines":102,"startLine":1,"totalLines":102}}}

The core file defining all extension point interfaces is pkg/scheduler/framework/interface.go, which contains the following interface definitions:\\n\\n1. PreFilterPlugin (line 512) and PreFilterExtensions (line 501): These define the PreFilter extension point where plugins run at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. PreFilterExtensions allows incremental updates through AddPod and RemovePod methods.\\n\\n2. FilterPlugin (line 540): Defines the Filter extension point for filtering out nodes that cannot run a pod. Replaces the old 'predicate' concept.\\n\\n3. PostFilterPlugin (line 561): Defines the PostFilter extension point called after a pod cannot be scheduled, typically used for preemption logic.\\n\\n4. PreScorePlugin (line 587): Defines the PreScore informational extension point called after filtering with the list of nodes that passed filtering.\\n\\n5. ScorePlugin (line 607) and ScoreExtensions (line 598): Define the Score extension point for ranking nodes. ScoreExtensions provides the NormalizeScore method for post-processing scores.\\n\\n6. ReservePlugin (line 624): Defines the Reserve extension point with Reserve and Unreserve methods for updating plugin state. Corresponds to the old 'assume' concept.\\n\\n7. PreBindPlugin (line 640): Defines the PreBind extension point called before binding a pod.\\n\\n8. PermitPlugin (line 660): Defines the Permit extension point called before binding with the ability to wait or prevent binding.\\n\\n9. BindPlugin (line 673): Defines the Bind extension point for binding a pod to a node.\\n\\n10. PostBindPlugin (line 649): Defines the PostBind extension point called after successful binding, used for cleanup.\\n\\nThe Framework interface (line 686) defines the top-level interface that manages all these plugins.\\n\\nThe runtime implementation in pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/framework.go contains the frameworkImpl struct that implements the Framework interface.
